% Custom commands for story placement using TikZ for rounded corners
\newcommand{\storybox}[3]{% #1=x, #2=y, #3=text
  \begin{textblock}{3}(#1,#2)
    \noindent%
    \begin{tikzpicture}
      \node[rectangle, rounded corners=3pt, fill=white, inner sep=0.1in, text width=2.55in, align=left] {%
        \small\sffamily #3%
      };
    \end{tikzpicture}%
  \end{textblock}%
}

\vspace{0.5in}

{\large\sffamily A Procedurally Generated Novel}

{\large\sffamily by Mark Sample}

\vfill

{\normalsize\sffamily Generated November 23, 2025}

% About page
\newpage
\section*{About This Novel}

\noindent\textit{No Time to Discourse} is a speculative atlas that explores climate disaster across North America through interactive mapping and generative flash fiction.

\vspace{0.3in}

This novel was generated for NaNoGenMo (National Novel Generation Month), transforming the web-based interactive experience into a print format. Each page combines watercolor maps from Stamen Design with procedurally-generated stories created through RiTa.js grammars.

\vspace{0.3in}

Each of the stories in this novel is a work of fiction, yet each also attempts to capture at a human level the realities of climate disaster.

\vspace{0.3in}

\textbf{Original Web Project:} \url{https://notime.now/}

\textbf{Code Repository:} \url{https://github.com/samplereality/no-time-to-discourse-novel}

\clearpage

% Henry V quote on its own page
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
  {\Large\textit{"The day is hot, and the weather, and the wars, and the King,\\
  and the Dukes; it is no time to discourse."}}

  \vspace{0.3in}

  --- Henry V
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\storybox{1.15}{4.53}{\textbf{Quesnel, British Columbia}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Saturday, April 21, 2029}\\
 Jade's apartment was burned to the ground. The fire spread like an furious wall of flames. She remembers the most random things. A laser pointer. An egg timer. Snail shells. All lost. Sunsets are achingly beautiful now.}

\storybox{2.25}{7.94}{\textbf{Williams Lake, British Columbia}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Wednesday, January 17, 2029}\\
 Scarlette's condo was destroyed. The fire spread like an furious tide of flames. She remembers the most random things. A magazine. A wristwatch. Egg timers. All lost. Is it the smoke that makes it hard to breathe?}

\storybox{0.95}{0.85}{\textbf{Prince George, British Columbia}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, May 14, 2029}\\
 Izaiah hears on the radio that dozens are injured as relentless water swamps Spruceland Mall. Jefferson lost everything, and no one knows how to help. Authorities have yet to declare a state of emergency. }

\storybox{5.38}{8.07}{\textbf{Hot Springs, Arkansas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, February 28, 2028}\\
 Alaya races home, feverishly hoping her daughter has already escaped. But she can't even get within 15 miles of Hot Springs. Police turn her away. She numbly watches the firestorm from the Ring camera on her front door, until the feed goes dead.}

\storybox{5.44}{4.74}{\textbf{Little Rock, Arkansas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Friday, August 3, 2029}\\
 ``It's a scorcher today,'' they say. Today? You mean this year. The August heat hits Elle fast and hard. Confusion, seizures. Nonsense thoughts drift through her head. \textit{Google Nest, Archer Daniel Midlands, Smokeless Nonevents.}}

\storybox{2.01}{7.10}{\textbf{Conway, Arkansas}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Sunday, 1:09 pm}\\
You stare numbly at the screen, your sallow face awash in blue light of your phone. Doomscrolling, to bring on the doom. There's no call to action on the map. But should you need one?}

\storybox{0.88}{1.01}{\textbf{Johnstown, Pennsylvania}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Friday, January 2, 2026}\\
 The streams are empty, and the earth lies barren in mute desolation. Gnarled roots broil  in the scorching sun. The towns are dead. It's like the surface of the moon, thinks Drake. It's been eleven months since rain. Dust blows in the air, clogging his throat.}

\storybox{4.25}{0.79}{\textbf{Altoona, Pennsylvania}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Wednesday, May 5, 2027}\\
 The earth withers, and the wells run dry. Dying fish bake  in the  sun. It's like the surface of the moon, thinks Anahi. It hasn't rained in weeks and weeks. The livestock are decimated. She stands there in a fog.}

\storybox{0.88}{4.22}{\textbf{State College, Pennsylvania}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Thursday, January 25, 2029}\\
 The reservoirs run dry, and a thick layer of dust covers the dorms. The remains of boats bake bare in the scorching sun. The livestock are decimated. It's something out of a post-apocalyptic movie, thinks Giana. It hasn't rained in weeks and weeks. The data center's cooling systems run 24/7, mining crypto.}

\storybox{5.47}{6.47}{\textbf{Cat Lake, Ontario}\\[0.1in]

 The storm had been building for days. The barometer was dropping. The air was heavy. When the storm finally came to Cat Lake, it was devastating. Kyleigh watched as the storm lashed against her windows. Meanwhile Pearl taps open Instagram, watching video after frenzied video revealing the truth about EMF weapons. Three hours pass.}

\storybox{1.77}{7.52}{\textbf{Red Lake, Ontario}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Friday, May 21, 2027}\\
 ``You could fry an egg on the sidewalk,'' they say. No. Not when the sidewalk itself is melting. The tracks near Red Lake buckle, a sun kink it's called, and all rail travel stops for the week. The ambient sound of ten thousand air conditioners washes over the land.}

\storybox{2.49}{3.22}{\textbf{Kenora, Ontario}\\[0.1in]

 Hurricane Isabella intensified over the warm Gulf waters, following the path forecasters feared most. Isabella evacuated to a shelter with hundreds of strangers with only what fit in the car. She stared at satellite images, begging God her 90-year-old oak tree would survive. Coast Guard helicopters plucked her from her roof at dawn. On social media the President bragged about his new plane.}
